I am thinking...: Based on my research, in Kubernetes v1.32, the CNI plugin code has been completely removed from the kubelet. The CNI integration is now entirely handled by the container runtime (containerd, CRI-O, etc.) via the CRI interface.

The key files that implement the CNI integration in kubernetes/kubernetes v1.32 are:

1. **CRI API** - The interface that defines how the runtime should handle networking:
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/services.go` - Defines `RuntimeService` interface with `RunPodSandbox`, `StopPodSandbox`, `UpdateRuntimeConfig`
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.pb.go` - Protocol buffer definitions
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/constants.go` - Constants like `NetworkReady`

2. **CRI Client** - The client that calls the CRI runtime:
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go` - Implements `RunPodSandbox`, `StopPodSandbox`, `UpdateRuntimeConfig`

3. **Kubelet kuberuntime** - The kubelet code that coordinates pod creation:
   - `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go` - `createPodSandbox`, `generatePodSandboxConfig`
   - `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go` - `SyncPod`, `UpdatePodCIDR`
   - `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go` - `NetworkNamespaceForPod`, `NamespacesForPod`

4. **Kubelet network** - Network state management:
   - `pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go` - `updatePodCIDR`
   - `pkg/kubelet/runtime.go` - `runtimeState` with network state management
   - `pkg/kubelet/errors.go` - Network error constants

5. **Kubelet container** - Container runtime interface:
   - `pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go` - `NetworkReady` constant, `Runtime` interface

2652026-03-08T19:39:36.826483agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Based on my extensive research, I can now compile a comprehensive list of files that implement the CNI (Container Network Interface) integration in kubernetes/kubernetes v1.32.

In Kubernetes v1.32, the CNI integration has been moved to the container runtime (containerd, CRI-O, etc.) via the CRI (Container Runtime Interface). The kubelet itself doesn't directly call CNI - instead it calls the CRI runtime which then calls CNI.

The key files that implement the CNI integration in kubernetes/kubernetes v1.32 are:

**CRI API (defines the interface for CNI integration):**
1. `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.proto` - Protocol buffer definitions for RunPodSandbox, StopPodSandbox, UpdateRuntimeConfig, NetworkConfig, PodSandboxNetworkStatus
2. `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.pb.go` - Generated Go code from the proto file
3. `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/constants.go` - NetworkReady, RuntimeReady constants
4. `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/services.go` - RuntimeService interface with RunPodSandbox, StopPodSandbox, UpdateRuntimeConfig

**CRI Client (implements the CRI client that calls the runtime):**
5. `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go` - remoteRuntimeService implementing RunPodSandbox, StopPodSandbox, UpdateRuntimeConfig

**Kubelet kuberuntime (coordinates CNI calls during pod creation):**

{
  "thought": "Based on my research, in Kubernetes v1.32, the CNI plugin code has been completely removed from the kubelet. The CNI integration is now entirely handled by the container runtime (containerd, CRI-O, etc.) via the CRI interface.\n\nThe key files that implement the CNI integration in kubernetes/kubernetes v1.32 are:\n\n1. **CRI API** - The interface that defines how the runtime should handle networking:\n   - `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/services.go` - Defines `RuntimeService` interface with `RunPodSandbox`, `StopPodSandbox`, `UpdateRuntimeConfig`\n   - `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.pb.go` - Protocol buffer definitions\n   - `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/constants.go` - Constants like `NetworkReady`\n\n2. **CRI Client** - The client that calls the CRI runtime:\n   - `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go` - Implements `RunPodSandbox`, `StopPodSandbox`, `UpdateRuntimeConfig`\n\n3. **Kubelet kuberuntime** - The kubelet code that coordinates pod creation:\n   - `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go` - `createPodSandbox`, `generatePodSandboxConfig`\n   - `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go` - `SyncPod`, `UpdatePodCIDR`\n   - `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go` - `NetworkNamespaceForPod`, `NamespacesForPod`\n\n4. **Kubelet network** - Network state management:\n   - `pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go` - `updatePodCIDR`\n   - `pkg/kubelet/runtime.go` - `runtimeState` with network state management\n   - `pkg/kubelet/errors.go` - Network error constants\n\n5. **Kubelet container** - Container runtime interface:\n   - `pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go` - `NetworkReady` constant, `Runtime` interface\n\nHowever, the task specifically asks about:\n- CNI plugin invocation\n- Network namespace setup\n- IP address management (IPAM) call\n- Network plugin manager that coordinates CNI calls during pod creation\n\nThese are all things that were in the old kubelet network plugin code. In v1.32, these are handled by the container runtime, not the kubelet.\n\nLet me look at the CRI API more carefully to understand what's relevant. The `RunPodSandbox` call is what triggers CNI plugin invocation in the container runtime. The `UpdateRuntimeConfig` call is what passes the pod CIDR to the network plugin (IPAM).\n\nLet me also look at the kuberuntime sandbox code more carefully to understand the network namespace setup."

It is currently part of LinuxPodSandboxConfig. In future, if we have securityContext pulled out\n// in podSandboxConfig we should be able to use it.\nfunc (m *kubeGenericRuntimeManager) generatePodSandboxLinuxConfig(pod *v1.Pod) (*runtimeapi.LinuxPodSandboxConfig, error) {\n        cgroupParent := m.runtimeHelper.GetPodCgroupParent(pod)\n        lc := &runtimeapi.LinuxPodSandboxConfig{\n                CgroupParent: cgroupParent,\n                SecurityContext: &runtimeapi.LinuxSandboxSecurityContext{\n                        Privileged: kubecontainer.HasPrivilegedContainer(pod),\n\n                        // Forcing sandbox to run as `runtime/default` allow users to\n                        // use least privileged seccomp profiles at pod level.            }\n                if sc.SupplementalGroups != nil {\n                        for _, sg := range sc.SupplementalGroups {\n wc := &runtimeapi.WindowsPodSandboxConfig{\n                SecurityContext: &runtimeapi.WindowsSandboxSecurityContext{},\n        }\n\n        if }\n\n                if !kubecontainer.IsHostNetworkPod(pod) {\n                        return nil, fmt.Errorf(\"hostNetwork is required if Pod contains HostProcess containers\")\n                }\n\n                wc.SecurityContext.HostProcess = true\n        }\n\n        sc := pod.Spec.SecurityContext\n        if sc == nil || sc.WindowsOptions == nil {\n                return wc, nil\n runtimeapi.PodSandboxState_SANDBOX_READY\n                filter = &runtimeapi.PodSandboxFilter{\n                        State: &runtimeapi.PodSandboxStateValue{\n sandbox.\nfunc (m *kubeGenericRuntimeManager) determinePodSandboxIPs(podNamespace, podName string, podSandbox *runtimeapi.PodSandboxStatus) []string {\n        podIPs := make([]string, 0)\n        if podSandbox.Network == nil {\n                klog.InfoS(\"Pod Sandbox status doesn't have network information, cannot report IPs\", \"pod\", klog.KRef(podNamespace, podName))\n                return podIPs\n        }\n\n        // ip could be an empty string if runtime is not responsible for the\n        // IP (e.g., host networking).\n\n        // pick primary IP\n        if \"pod\", klog.KRef(podNamespace, podName), \"IP\", podSandbox.Network.Ip)\n                        return nil\n                }\n                podIPs = append(podIPs, podSandbox.Network.Ip)\n            return nil, nil\n        }\n\n        // Sort with newest first.\n        sandboxIDs := make([]string, len(sandboxes))\n        sort.Sort(podSandboxByCreated(sandboxes))\n        for i, s := range sandboxes {\n                sandboxIDs[i] = s.Id\n        }\n\n        return sandboxIDs, nil\n}\n\n// GetPortForward gets the endpoint the runtime will serve the port-forward request
